## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the population growth rate (dP/dt) as a function of time (t) and current population size (P). This is a classic population dynamics problem where growth rate depends on population size through various density-dependent and density-independent mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Exponential (Malthusian) growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P', 'scenario': 'Density-independent growth where rate is proportional to population size'}
- {'name': 'Logistic growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P)', 'scenario': 'Density-dependent growth with carrying capacity'}
- {'name': 'Gompertz growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P)', 'scenario': 'Growth that decelerates logarithmically as population approaches carrying capacity'}
- {'name': 'Theta-logistic growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)', 'scenario': 'Generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence'}
- {'name': 'Allee effect growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P)', 'scenario': 'Growth with both a minimum viable population (Allee threshold) and carrying capacity'}
- {'name': 'Von Bertalanffy-type growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P', 'scenario': 'Growth as balance between anabolic (power-law) and catabolic (linear) processes'}
- {'name': 'Richards growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) / c2', 'scenario': 'Flexible sigmoidal growth generalizing logistic and Gompertz'}
- {'name': 'Power-law growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**c1', 'scenario': 'Allometric scaling of growth rate with population size'}
- {'name': 'Time-dependent exponential growth', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t)', 'scenario': 'Growth rate with time-varying intrinsic rate (e.g., seasonal or environmental change)'}
- {'name': 'Beverton-Holt continuous analog', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P', 'scenario': 'Density-dependent birth rate with constant per-capita mortality'}
- {'name': 'Logistic with time-dependent carrying capacity', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t))', 'scenario': 'Logistic growth where carrying capacity changes over time'}
- {'name': 'Quadratic density dependence', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2', 'scenario': 'Polynomial approximation of density-dependent growth'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent regulation → multiplicative factor (1 - P/K) or similar terms that reduce growth as P increases
- Allee effects (cooperative behavior at low density) → cubic terms in P, e.g., P*(P-a)*(K-P), producing negative growth at very low P
- Gompertz-type deceleration → logarithmic terms log(K/P) providing slower approach to carrying capacity than logistic
- Metabolic scaling in populations → fractional power laws P**c with c ≠ 1, reflecting allometric relationships
- Time-explicit environmental forcing → multiplicative or additive functions of t (e.g., sinusoidal, exponential) modulating intrinsic growth rate
- Equilibrium/steady-state identification → dP_dt = 0 at specific P values reveals carrying capacity and other fixed points
- Ratio of polynomial orders in P determines number of equilibria → degree-n polynomial in P yields up to n fixed points
- Separable vs non-separable structure → if dP_dt depends only on P (not t), the ODE is autonomous; time-dependence signals external forcing

**Candidate 48:** `P*(c0*(P*c1-1)*((P*c2)^c3-1) + c4*(P+c5)*(P*c6+1))`
Expanding: c0 term gives P*c0*(P*c1-1)*(c2^c3*P^c3-1). Set c3=1/3: P*c0*(P*c1-1)*(c2^(1/3)*P^(1/3)-1). This gives terms like P^(4/3), P^(7/3), P², P. The c4 term gives P*c4*(P+c5)*(P*c6+1) = c4*c6*P³ + c4*(1+c5*c6)*P² + c4*c5*P. So total has P³, P², P, P^(7/3), P^(4/3), P^(1/3) (from expanding). We need P^(7/3) and P^(4/3) coefficients to be 0 while keeping P^(1/3) nonzero. Let me expand:

P*c0*(P*c1-1)*(c2^(1/3)*P^(1/3)-1) = c0*P*(c1*c2^(1/3)*P^(4/3) - c1*P - c2^(1/3)*P^(1/3) + 1)
= c0*c1*c2^(1/3)*P^(7/3) - c0*c1*P² - c0*c2^(1/3)*P^(4/3) + c0*P

For P^(7/3) = 0: c0*c1*c2^(1/3) = 0. If c0=0, entire first part vanishes. If c1=0: then first part = c0*P*(-1)*(c2^(1/3)*P^(1/3)-1) = c0*P - c0*c2^(1/3)*P^(4/3). Still has P^(4/3). If c2=0: first part = c0*P*(c1*P*(-1)-(-1)) = c0*P*(-c1*P+1) = -c0*c1*P² + c0*P. No P^(1/3).

Can't get P^(1/3) without unwanted fractional powers.
